  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_51b1735a-5a4e-4e9b-aa3c-b95a132dd3d0'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15880150032140608379"><i>Her story is a phenomenon. Her life is a disaster.</i><br/><br/>In the real world, Eliza Mirk is shy, weird, and friendless. Online, she’s LadyConstellation, the anonymous creator of the wildly popular webcomic <i>Monstrous Sea</i>.   <span id="freeText15880150032140608379" style="display:none"><i>Her story is a phenomenon. Her life is a disaster.</i><br /><br />In the real world, Eliza Mirk is shy, weird, and friendless. Online, she’s LadyConstellation, the anonymous creator of the wildly popular webcomic <i>Monstrous Sea</i>. Eliza can’t imagine enjoying the real world as much as she loves the online one, and she has no desire to try.<br /><br />Then Wallace Warland, <i>Monstrous Sea</i>’s biggest fanfiction writer, transfers to her school. Wallace thinks Eliza is just another fan, and as he draws her out of her shell, she begins to wonder if a life offline might be worthwhile.<br /><br />But when Eliza’s secret is accidentally shared with the world, everything she’s built—her story, her relationship with Wallace, and even her sanity—begins to fall apart.</span>

<div id="review_1864467743" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864467743" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864467743?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864467743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972319459923035998"><blockquote>
  <i> She drew so many monsters that she became a monster herself.</i>
</blockquote><br/>4 1/2 stars. The only reason it's not 5 is that it took a little while for me to get into it. But when I did, <b>it completely blew me away</b>. I liked this even more than Zappia's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up' title='Made You Up by Francesca Zappia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Made You Up</a>.<br/><br/>I'm not going to lie to you - a huge part of my love for this book is because I related so much to Eliza. So freaking much. Well, except for the part where she's a talented webcomic artist and I'm not, but shhh. <br/><br/>Some of you know this, but others do</span>
  <span id="freeText6972319459923035998" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i> She drew so many monsters that she became a monster herself.</i>
</blockquote><br />4 1/2 stars. The only reason it's not 5 is that it took a little while for me to get into it. But when I did, <b>it completely blew me away</b>. I liked this even more than Zappia's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up" title="Made You Up by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Made You Up</a>.<br /><br />I'm not going to lie to you - a huge part of my love for this book is because I related so much to Eliza. So freaking much. Well, except for the part where she's a talented webcomic artist and I'm not, but shhh. <br /><br />Some of you know this, but others don't-- I have long suffered with anxiety, particularly social anxiety. I get worked up about sending emails, angsting over it when replies don't come straight away (<i>oh god, did I say something wrong?</i>). I literally used to drink alcohol before the mandatory presentations in college (not showing up only worked for so long), and I still feel panic rising inside me whenever I have to make a phone call to someone I don't know well. Over the years, I've come to handle it better; to talk myself down from the panic. But it's still there.<br /><br />It's been part of who I am my whole life. From my very first school years when I almost always played alone, to later bullying because I was that "weird" and socially clueless class member who didn't get how to behave. And the way I coped? To put it simply - <b>The Internet</b>. The Internet provided a place for me to explore the world, find others like me, whilst also providing a barrier. I was invisible, free, and not alone in the way I was often alone in the real world. <br /><br />I spent hours every night on my computer, until my parents got frustrated that I spent so much time alone and not in the "real world". What they didn't get - and what Eliza's parents don't get in this book - is that I wasn't alone. I was making friends from all over the world. And they were better friends than any I'd had in "real life" at that point. And, as Eliza says:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>It’s stupid because that’s what I like about the internet—that it gives you time to think about what you want to say before you say it. </i>
</blockquote><br /><b>It's always so wonderful to find a book that "gets" you</b>. A book that puts into words feelings you've always had but have struggled to voice. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31931941.Eliza_and_Her_Monsters" title="Eliza and Her Monsters by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Eliza and Her Monsters</a> did just that.<br /><br />From my perspective, it's a very realistic portrayal of anxiety, and of someone who escapes into Internet forums. Eliza's most valued friendships are online and, of course, her well-meaning parents fail to understand or consider them "real".<br /><br />It's a <b>much darker book</b> than I was first expecting. While there is lots of geeky fandom, fanfiction, fanart, cosplay... the story of Eliza's anxiety, relationships with those around her, and even suicidal thoughts, gives the novel a more serious and emotional edge. I appreciate books like this, though. If you're looking for a geeky fandom book that is lighter and fluffier, I recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28245707.Queens_of_Geek" title="Queens of Geek by Jen Wilde" rel="nofollow noopener">Queens of Geek</a>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>There is a small monster in my brain that controls my doubt.<br />The doubt itself is a stupid thing, without sense or feeling, blind and straining at the end of a long chain. The monster, though, is smart. It’s always watching, and when I am completely sure of myself, it unchains the doubt and lets it run wild. Even when I know it’s coming, I can’t stop it.</i>
</blockquote><br />There's another layer to this book, too, which I found really interesting. As well as being about Eliza's anxiety, it's also about an issue that is becoming ever more relevant today, and it's an issue that I don't recall reading anything about before-- the relationship between an artist and their fans. Or, really, anyone with a fan following. <br /><br />As Eliza becomes more popular online, the thing she did for herself, for her own escapism, becomes about other people and what they expect from her. People start to expect a certain type of work and feel like her popularity means she owes the world (and them) something. This opens a fascinating discussion on what artists/writers/etc. owe their fans or followers. Whether, in fact, they owe them anything. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Creating art is a lonely task, which is why we introverts revel in it, but when we have fans looming over us, it becomes loneliness of a different sort. We become caged animals watched by zoo-goers, expected to perform lest the crowd grow bored or angry. It’s not always bad. Sometimes we do well, and the cage feels more like a pedestal.</i>
</blockquote><br />It was honestly <b>such an interesting and thoughtful book</b>. On many levels. It manages to be very emotionally moving, entertaining, beautifully-illustrated AND do something new at the same time. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31931941.Eliza_and_Her_Monsters" title="Eliza and Her Monsters by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Eliza and Her Monsters</a> deserves all of the hype.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6972319459923035998" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I actually think it lined up perfectly with something I'm facing in my own life right now, that's similar to what Eliza faced with being a creator online. I feel so connected and understood by this story and I'm glad I finally worked myself up to finishing it. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2699838351727898474">UPDATE: $2.99 Kindle US today 9/12/19<br/><br/><b>I got some wonderful stuff in the mail yesterday (7/3/17) and I love them! I love getting stuff from the pub etc.</b><br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499172740i/23200390._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><br/><b>I loved this book so very much!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495213165i/22797068._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*****There will be some spoilers because I can't help myself*****<br/><br/>I love the book has drawings and stories all through-out the book. They are so awesome! <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810736._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810737._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810738._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love Eliza. She's quiet, wants to be left alone in her online world where she writes her webcomic: Monstrous Sea. She has two wonderful friends online that have hel</span>
  <span id="freeText2699838351727898474" style="display:none">UPDATE: $2.99 Kindle US today 9/12/19<br><br><b>I got some wonderful stuff in the mail yesterday (7/3/17) and I love them! I love getting stuff from the pub etc.</b><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499172740i/23200390._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>I loved this book so very much!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495213165i/22797068._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*****There will be some spoilers because I can't help myself*****<br><br>I love the book has drawings and stories all through-out the book. They are so awesome! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810736._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810737._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495370170i/22810738._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Eliza. She's quiet, wants to be left alone in her online world where she writes her webcomic: Monstrous Sea. She has two wonderful friends online that have helped her with her business. There is Max who runs security on the trolls (we need him for GR) and Emmy who set up the merch for the comic and sales for the comic, etc. Eliza makes enough money to live off of and put her way through college. She famous and she's anonymous. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I do have friends. Maybe they live hundreds of miles away from me, and maybe I can only talk to them through a screen, but they're still my friends. They don't just hold Monstrous Sea together. They hold me together. <br><br>Max and Emmy are the reason any of this exists.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Eliza doesn't talk to people at school. Some people are actually afraid of her and she's happy with this because all she want's is to draw out her next parts for the comic during school. Then when she gets home she puts the drawings and stuff on her photoshop to get it complete and uploads them. <br><br>God, I wish I could draw and do something so freaking cool like that. Anyhoo . . . <br><br>Eliza isn't really close to her parents. They are always trying to get her to do sports and random stuff she has no interest in. They think her comic is a hobby, she never told them how famous or how much money she makes. They think she makes a little bit of money and just let her do it. I do wish that Eliza would have been up front with them and I do wish that her parents would have taken the time to actually go online and read her comic and see how famous she actually was, but none of this happened. And later on, it bites them all in the butt. <br><br>Eliza has two brothers: Church and Sully. She doesn't do much with them because they are into sports etc. She has no idea that they follow her comic and so do their friends. And when Church takes up for Eliza when her parent do something extremely stupid, I was so proud. I mean so proud. He put them in their place once and for all because sometimes parents aren't always right, even if they mean well. <br><br>I must also mention that I'm in love with Davy, their Great Pyrenees =) <br><br>Moving on. <br><br>Eliza meets the new kid at school, Wallace. He starts writing notes to her because he doesn't really like to talk. It's really super cute and he's freaking hot. Just sayin'. It turns out that he writes fanfiction for Eliza's comic! <br><br>They become close and start going out which is way beyond anything Eliza has ever done in her life! I think they are wonderful together but she never tells him that she is LadyConstellation and the creator of Monstrous Sea. I wanted to scream! He finds out when every one else does when her parents do something stupid. Poor Emmy and Max have to try to fight and keep everyone off Eliza's back and even Church cusses people to leave her alone. Eliza has a breakdown after her cover is blown and doesn't even want to finish her comic. She has to see a counselor and take anxiety meds, it's all just one big mess. If her parents would have just butted out and if Eliza would have just told them how big she is. . . so many things. <br><br>Wallace gets mad at her obviously. I mean she should have told him but it is what it is. He gets even more mad at her when she decides she's not going to finish the comic because he has an offer to get his fan fiction published. It could make his dreams come true as well. I find it strange that people can make money off other people's work but I guess that's life. <br><br>Some drastic things make everything come to a close and the world to be complete again. Eliza is even closer to her family and things are awesome with Wallace. It was a happy ending for all involved. <br><br>I really wish this book would continue or maybe a little novella of what happens with everyone later on. <br><br>This book was so awesome to me and it meant a lot on so many levels. It's a really great thing when a book can make you feel so good. Fin<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/05/eliza-and-her-monsters-by-francesca.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2699838351727898474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2017229944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2017229944" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2017229944?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=diverse">diverse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-and-a-half-stars">1-and-a-half-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=library">library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2017229944" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13630877719820281636">in a friendly reminder that i've sh*t on all your faves, i posted this review!! find it here (preferably before unfollowing me out of righteous fury): <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/05/22/books-everyone-liked-and-i-did-not-more-unpopular-opinions/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>------------<br/>Hindsight is 20/20.<br/><br/>I now understand, having read this book, what I did not grasp previously: that maybe I shouldn’t have expected to like this. <br/><br/>For one thing, I full on hate Francesca Zappia’s other book with everything that I am, which in retrospect is seeming like a more important factor than i</span>
  <span id="freeText13630877719820281636" style="display:none">in a friendly reminder that i've sh*t on all your faves, i posted this review!! find it here (preferably before unfollowing me out of righteous fury): <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/05/22/books-everyone-liked-and-i-did-not-more-unpopular-opinions/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />------------<br />Hindsight is 20/20.<br /><br />I now understand, having read this book, what I did not grasp previously: that maybe I shouldn’t have expected to like this. <br /><br />For one thing, I full on hate Francesca Zappia’s other book with everything that I am, which in retrospect is seeming like a more important factor than it did at the time.<br /><br />I also really, really hate my-big-secret-was-revealed-and-now-everyone-in-high-school-knows-and-my-life-is-ruined-in-a-very-quintessentially-high-school-way plotlines. They are so stressful.<br /><br />But I like contemporaries! And I like the Internet! And I like illustrations! And I like mental illness rep! And I like books people like! (That first and last one are blatantly false, but still.)<br /><br />I had hope, is what I’m saying.<br /><br />This book crushed every last BIT of that.<br /><br />As I just ranted about (except not actually because it’ll probably take me a million years to post this, even after it took me a million years to write it, even after it took me a million years to read the book) in my review of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2056227527?type=review#rating_146254213" rel="nofollow noopener">Everything All at Once</a>, <i>I am sick to death of the sh*tty family trope.</i><br /><br />But I didn’t realize just how sick of it I could be, just how hard that trope could scrape against the bottom of the entertainment barrel, just how low we could get, until I read this book.<br /><br />THIS BOOK HAS PERHAPS THE WORST FAMILY DYNAMIC OF ANY BOOK I’VE EVER READ. Because not only is it grueling and dramatic and boring and done, it’s also completely nonsensical.<br /><br />Eliza has two little brothers, who are so flat and annoying they actually go well past the bounds of the very definitions of the words “flat” and “annoying.” She does not get along well with said brothers, and is, in fact, quite mean to them despite being many years older and, one would suppose (incorrectly), more mature. So that’s awesome.<br /><br />But we don’t get to the very limits of terrible until we talk about Eliza’s parents. That statement, along with every single statement made in this book, may lead you to assume that Eliza’s parents are the problem. However, every single cell in my entire body vehemently disagrees with that assumption.<br /><br />Eliza’s parents are just two people trying their best!!!!!! Their daughter never talks to them and spends her whole life in her room, on the Internet, and they don’t know what to do about it which is not exactly shocking considering Eliza never talks to them!!!!! They’re just trying to parent!!!!!<br /><br />I think this book may have been designed to appeal to the children of technology. Here is a girl who has it all, in terms of what the online world can offer: she has anxiety, but she’s unbelievably famous, has swarms of online friends, creates amazing art, gets a boyfriend. What goes along with that is the inevitable disapproving parental figure is actually - gasp! - wrong. <br /><br />Maybe that’s another reason I was destined not to like this book: I firmly believe you can’t be on the internet all the time. Not even if your friends are on there, not even if your job is on there, not even if, like, a goddamn opportunity to hook up with Zac Efron is on there. Which I guess it is, technically speaking. REGARDLESS OF THE CIRCUMSTANCES, the real world matters too, is what I’m saying.<br /><br />I firmly believe that Eliza should have apologized to her parents. She doesn’t talk to them unless she’s spewing vitriol, she ignores her family, she stays in her room all the time, she refuses to even offer an explanation as to why all of this would be okay. Once she does - sorry, once her brothers do <i>for her</i> - good ol’ mom and dad are more than understanding.<br /><br />I gave this book the benefit of the doubt for <i>SO LONG</i> because I thought character development would change the way she treats her family but nOOO, HER PARENTS WERE ACTUALLY IN THE WRONG ALL ALONG, AND IN TURN SO WAS I, MOTHER AND FATHER AND I ARE JUST THREE MORE FOOLS INHABITING THIS WORLD OF FURY AND NONSENSE.<br /><br />Not even the fun Alice’s Adventures in Wonderland kind.<br /><br />In the abundant free time Eliza doesn’t spend creating an inexplicably famous and successful web comic or ruining the lives of her family members, she’s living it up sexual tension-wise with a kid named Wallace.<br /><br />I support this relationship, but only because Eliza and Wallace both suck so equally that they were probably made for each other. They treat each other like sh*t, and Wallace is so boring. Like seriously. Guys. This is your MCM?<br /><br />Eliza stupidly hides the fact that she writes that massively successful web comic from Wallace, even though Wallace is a huge fan of it and talks to her about it all the time and revealed <i>his</i> secret online identity to <i>her</i>. But whatever, of course that is what would happen in a book this trope-y.<br /><br />HOWEVER. Here’s the thing. Eliza and Wallace write notes to each other <u>all the time</u> (like straight up instead of talking). Eliza also handwrites the speech bubbles for her comic, which Wallace is obsessed with. Like photographic-memory-level-of-knowledge obsessed. <i>Can Wallace not recognize handwriting?</i> There’s a moment when Eliza recognizes Wallace’s after seeing it ONE TIME.<br /><br />This book is dumb and I hate it.<br /><br />Good mental illness rep, though. If only everything else didn’t suck so hard.<br /><br />Bottom line: This book is designed to speak to its audience, and that high-as-hell average rating tells me it worked. BUT NOT FOR ME. SORRY, FOLKS.<br /><br />------------<br />PRE-REVIEW<br /><br />Guys…<br /><br />I mean...come on.<br /><br />Like...what the ever-living hell…?<br /><br />God.<br /><br />Review to come</span>
  <a data-text-id="13630877719820281636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2340694226" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2340694226" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2340694226?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2340694226" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4108702565923385632"><b>3.8</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote> “You found me in a constellation.” <br/><br/>― Francesca Zappia, Eliza and Her Monsters </blockquote><br/><br/>This book was an adequate distraction from my real life right now. Which is exams, pressure, exams, kill me, exams, fuck-my-life, death. I enjoyed reading 50 pages of this every day before I went to sleep after a stressful and straining day. <br/><br/>We start off with Eliza, an unsociable, shy and introverted high school girl who is experiencing anxiety and depression and is closed off to the virtual wor</span>
  <span id="freeText4108702565923385632" style="display:none"><b>3.8</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote> “You found me in a constellation.” <br /><br />― Francesca Zappia, Eliza and Her Monsters </blockquote><br /><br />This book was an adequate distraction from my real life right now. Which is exams, pressure, exams, kill me, exams, fuck-my-life, death. I enjoyed reading 50 pages of this every day before I went to sleep after a stressful and straining day. <br /><br />We start off with Eliza, an unsociable, shy and introverted high school girl who is experiencing anxiety and depression and is closed off to the virtual world of the Internet. She is, also, the Anonymous creator of the most popular web comic <i> Monstrous Sea </i> which is read by millions and millions of people all over the world. Then she meets Wallace, the most popular fan fiction writer of her comic, who is transferred to her school and then everything changes. <br /><br />This book didn't give me feels. This book didn't make me cling to my seat to read what happens next. These characters didn't pull me as much as I would have hoped. This feeling probably comes to me when I read a book in two or three sittings and probably this book didn't give me this intense feeling of desperation to finish it because I was reading it during a tough time. But it was probably just the book. This was a book with a great anxiety representation, amazing artwork throughout done by the author, and a very interesting storyline. But that's about it.<br /><br />The only characters I liked were Eliza and Wallace. All the others just... didn't exist to me. They felt more flat than fucking flat-Earthers think the Earth is. Her parents, her brothers, Wallace's friends, his family... didn't do it for me. Eliza didn't pay much attention to people, especially in the beginning, and that's why I think her POV story didn't make me relate to these characters on no level at all. <br /><br />The romance was very cute and fluffy, I really enjoyed how awkwardly they started off and how they were writing everything in little notes but after it became canon it got lost to me. It's one of those ships that you're dying to happen but when it does, you're totally uninterested by it. But they shared a deep relationship and I'm so glad they found each other. We all closed off people who love books, tv shows, movie e.t.c. too much need people like this in our lives.<br /><br />I hate the everything-is-turning-out-amazing-and-nothing-is-wrong-and-everything-was-shit-as-fuck-throughout-the book-and-then-after-a-while-everything-solves-itself trope. And it happened here, in some way. I don't want my characters to struggle, but I'm a realist. And I enjoy realistic endings and situations in books. And I don't enjoy when literally everything is upside down and glum and sad and depressing and then it all just... poof! Gone! And I'm not talking about financial problems which can be solved with a good new job or anything but emotional ones. This book didn't leave this taste entirely to me but it did in certain aspects. And I didn't enjoy that.<br /><br />This novel was very much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16068905.Fangirl" title="Fangirl by Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Fangirl</a>, plot-wise but also not much . They were written in the same format, both the protagonists were young white straight girls who were popular on the Internet, both of them had anxiety, each chapter we got a snippet from their work e.t.c. This might be an unpopular opinion, I don't know... I enjoyed Fangirl more. It had its flaws and they were many but the characters gripped me more. Characters do it for me in books, if I don't desperately till I fucking die love the characters, or if I don't furiously want to kill any of them till they bleed right in front of me, the book feels neutral to me. The plot might be legendary but if the characters are bad or if I don't relate to them, my dick won't move. I need to receive these strong feelings from books. I'm an all or nothing kind of person, nothing to do about it. <br /><br />And now off to what I enjoyed... I adored the world of <i> Monstrous Sea </i>, I love it when writers explore more worlds within one book of theirs, I adored the fandom aspect, the artwork throughout, the little text messages Eliza had with her online friends. It was a very interesting and quick paced YA contemporary and it kept me a nice company. I would truly recommend it to people who love YA contemporary books. And till the next one... K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4108702565923385632" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2014910230" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2014910230" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2014910230?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10067920-samantha?shelf=favorites-2017">favorites-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2014910230" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16289584532169198296">I just binge read this in a day. No regrets. 4.5 stars. <br/><br/>As someone who isn't the biggest fan of contemporary, THIS is the kind of contemporary for me. It's a celebration of fandom and online life. It's like Fangirl on steroids. It deals with mental health, and negativity online beautifully. AND, one of the fandoms the protagonist was a part of is actually a real serial novel the author puts up on Wattpad and Tumblr. So cool. This is a love letter to fandom and I ADORED it. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1931573521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931573521" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1931573521?book_show_action=true">Aug 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">all contemporary fans, especially teens and parents of teens</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2017">y-out2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=this-gave-me-hope-for-humanity">this-gave-me-hope-for-humanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mental-illness-disability">mental-illness-disability</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trauma-abuse-recovery">trauma-abuse-recovery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1931573521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer65016721800705805"><blockquote>
  <b><i>I understand that it's a teenage thing to say parents don't get it, but they</i> don't get it. <i>It's not their fault they were born two and a half decades before me, but would it kill the to ask me what I'm doing on the phone before they assume it's something pointless?</i></b>
</blockquote><b>
  <u>This is maybe one of the best contemporaries I've ever read.</u>
</b> I mean, I read it in three sittings within the same five hours. Francesca Zappia: you're doing amazing, sweetie.<br/><br/><br/>♔ <b>THEMES AND MENTAL ILLNESS</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>What good is a care</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText65016721800705805" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b><i>I understand that it's a teenage thing to say parents don't get it, but they</i> don't get it. <i>It's not their fault they were born two and a half decades before me, but would it kill the to ask me what I'm doing on the phone before they assume it's something pointless?</i></b>
</blockquote><b>
  <u>This is maybe one of the best contemporaries I've ever read.</u>
</b> I mean, I read it in three sittings within the same five hours. Francesca Zappia: you're doing amazing, sweetie.<br /><br /><br />♔ <b>THEMES AND MENTAL ILLNESS</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>What good is a career that makes you money if you hate yourself every day you do it?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><b>This book is about how teenagers get dismissed.</b> Let me explain. Teens are vehicles for drama rather than being real people. Our feelings aren't feelings - they're drama, or teen angst. But what's the real difference when both of us are people, humans with emotions and feelings and moods and <i>lives?</i> It's rare to see the feelings of teenagers validated to this degree, explicitly treated as relevant by the narrative. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>If I have my phone out talking to you or my online friends, they think I'm ignoring them, or being disrespectful, or whatever. And it's like, no, I'm in the middle of a conversation. If you saw people talking to each other face to face, you wouldn't interrupt them and call it disrespectful, would you?</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> The other thing I really loved thematically was <b>the emphasis on online life as being a positive thing</b> for some teens. See, here's the thing - having a community online has had a positive impact on my life. I mean, before I started using the internet in maybe 2014, I was pretty much the most antisocial kid ever. I had approximately three friends and two feelings. And then came the discourse, the banter, the memes, and the friends. And I got life experiences. All jokes aside, my real life is much more engaging, humorous, and brave <i>because</i> of experiences I've had on the internet. And I've yet to see that acknowledged in any YA books I've read thus far. I think this is a book I would recommend to parents as much as teenagers, just for how immersed I was in Eliza's experiences. <br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Worth as a person is not based on any tangible evidence. There's no test for it, no scale.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />This is just... so important.<br /><br /><br />♔ <b>WHY THIS IS A FANTASTIC CONTEMPORARY</b><br /><br />Aside from mental health handling, this is really just a fantastic book. First of all, there's the <b>mixed media.</b> I loved the little posts spread throughout the book of Eliza's comic - I'm super interested in seeing the full thing now. If you liked those too, you can find a full written version of the webcomic <a href="https://www.wattpad.com/355572195-the-children-of-hypnos-chapter-1-dreamhunter" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>! I also thought the text-speak was way more realistic than usual. <br /><br />What's most important in a good contemporary for me is having interesting, well-developed characters. And here, I can definitely say that the <b>character work</b> is fabulous. Eliza's perspective as a girl with anxiety was superbly realistic and enjoyable. She's fantastically developed and her character arc felt especially real to me.<br /><br /><b>And I loved the romance!!</b> The love interest, Wallace, is super cute, and I loved their relationship development. It felt authentic and honest and romantic all at the same time. It's hard to write a romance so honestly, but this is just one of the better YA contemporary romances I've ever read. <br /><br />VERDICT: One of the best contemporaries I've read this year, with fantastic themes and characters. Oh god, I just want everyone to read it? please. read this. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="65016721800705805" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2060470141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060470141" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060470141?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060470141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15539104860826371524"><b>This is like the ultimate book for those of us who hiss at sunlight and live on the internet.</b> SO MUCH INTERNET APPRECIATION. I also absolutely <i>adored</i> the writing, the anxiety/depression rep, the themes of creating and art and writing, and how many illustrations were in this book. Like <i>so many illustrations</i>?!???? I'm so pleased.<br/><br/>I shall just hug it now.<br/><br/><b>I also really loved the author's debut <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up' title='Made You Up by Francesca Zappia' rel='nofollow noopener'>Made You Up</a>!</b> And like I couldn't help comparing them a little as I read...and I definitely loved MYU more. B</span>
  <span id="freeText15539104860826371524" style="display:none"><b>This is like the ultimate book for those of us who hiss at sunlight and live on the internet.</b> SO MUCH INTERNET APPRECIATION. I also absolutely <i>adored</i> the writing, the anxiety/depression rep, the themes of creating and art and writing, and how many illustrations were in this book. Like <i>so many illustrations</i>?!???? I'm so pleased.<br /><br />I shall just hug it now.<br /><br /><b>I also really loved the author's debut <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17661416.Made_You_Up" title="Made You Up by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Made You Up</a>!</b> And like I couldn't help comparing them a little as I read...and I definitely loved MYU more. But Eliza and Her Monsters was just so poignantly relatable. I felt really understood reading it and so many thoughts and feelings Eliza had were just like..."Okay wow this is creepy because this is me."<br /><br /><b>And you know what's best?! THE EMPHASIS ON INTERNET FRIENDS.</b> 98% of Eliza's life is online and her parents are like "ok but they're not real friends." LOL @ YOU PARENTS. Internet friends are fabulous and Eliza knew it. I adored the messages with Emmy and Max. I also really appreciated the age gap?! Like Emmy's 14 and Max is early 20s and Eliza is 17. <b>It underlined how you can be friends with all types of people online.</b> It's really sweet and nice. And the book totally did highlight how the internet can suck, but mostly it was positive which was such a refreshing change.<br /><br /><b>Also the CHARACTERS WERE DARLING. MAY I JUST FLAIL FOR A MOMENT? I SHALL.</b> Eliza most definitely had anxiety/depression and her whole LIFE was creating this super-famous webcomic series. Her family didn't take it seriously, but she was uber famous (and anonymous) online. I really loved that aspect!! Eliza also always wore baggy sweaters, tried to melt away in crowds, hardly ever spoke, and basically lived and breathed her passion. #Relatable <b>And then there was Wallace...precious cinnamon Wallace.</b> He has selective mutism and is like this huge guy you "expect" to be a football player but -- NO HE'S ACTUALLY A WRITER. And supercute. <b>He and Eliza start off as friends and then...moooore.</b> Their friendship = to romance was so well done. So shippable. They both had lots of anxiety issues, but their story was about art and learning how to trust someone enough to be friends and being passionate about things. It's a book with issues but it's not an issue book...and there's nothing wrong with issue books. I just prefer when people are <i>more</i>. These two so were. Cute and precious. &lt;3<br /><br />(I also really really really loved that it featured protagonists who weren't good at talking. They communicated through art and writing. It was SO good and SO well done.) (I mean, there is dialogue, but it just really showed this side to anxiety that often gets forgotten and I just ajfdksalfd.)<br /><br /><b>My only shrug comes at the plot...because I've read it before.</b> Several times, haha. It felt very very much like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30724132.Geekerella" title="Geekerella by Ashley Poston" rel="nofollow noopener">Geekerella</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25322449.Radio_Silence" title="Radio Silence by Alice Oseman" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16068905.Fangirl" title="Fangirl by Rainbow Rowell" rel="nofollow noopener">Fangirl</a>! So for me, I predicted everything and kind of lost the element of freshness.<br /><br /><b>BUT IT'S FULL OF ILLUSTRATIONS!!!</b> So that more than makes up for it. (Like woah legit the comics in the book are <i>so good</i>?!? This author is so madly and marvellously talented.<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: I loved the writing and the characters and the sheer amount of GEEK AND INTERNET LOVE.</b> I love how it really <i>got</i> me. I don't get that a lot in books! It didn't knock my socks off, but hey my socks are lovely where they are thanks. So I'm just glad I got to dive into this world of art and comics and writing and teens who create magical worlds to escape into.<br /><br />Also anytime someone says "exercise" Eliza runs away. This is relatable and perfect.<br /><br /><br />**** QUOTES ****<br /><br /><blockquote>It's stupid, but that's what I like about the internet -- that it gives you time to think about what you want to say before you say it.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Do you ever have an idea for a story, a character, or even a line of dialogue or something, and suddenly it seems like the whole world is brighter? Like everything opens up, and everything makes sense?"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>If I like a book, I devour it in one sitting, and then I forget a lot. It's fine with me, because I read them over and over again. But Wallace will take weeks to read a book -- shortened to days, if he really likes it -- and he remembers all of it, and then he doesn't read it again.</blockquote><br /><br />I AM OFFICIALLY ELIZA.<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>MirkerLurker: No, it's okay! You think way harder about stories than I do.<br />rainmaker: What do you read them for?<br />MirkerLurker: The characters, I guess. I thought the characters were the reason anyone read Monstrous Sea.<br />rainmaker: You mean like, shipping?<br />MirkerLurker: No, not shipping -- shipping's great, and I do it all the time, but I mean...the characters themselves. The struggles they have to go through, and when you relaly love them, how much the affect you. When the characters are good, they make you care about everything else. That's why I draw them. It probably sounds dumb, but they're like real people to me. And this will probably sound worse, but sometimes I like them better than real people. I can emphathize with characters. Real people are harder.<br />rainmaker: Real people don't have concise character arcs.<br />MirkerLurker: Yes, exactly.</blockquote><br /><br />(IT WAS AT THIS POINT I RELATED SO HARD I NEARLY CRIED TBH.)<br /><br /><blockquote>"If I have my phone out talking to you or my online friends, they think I'm ignoring them, or being disrespectful, or whatever. And it's like, no, I'm in the middle of a conversation. If you saw two people talking to each other face-to-face, you wouldn't interrupt them and call it disrespectful, would you?"</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Eliza, your worth as a person is not dependant on the art you create or what other people think of it."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="15539104860826371524" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3333914848" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3333914848" />
    <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named"><img alt="She-who-must-not-be-named " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602257813p2/106473614.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3333914848?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="user" itemprop="url" name="She-who-must-not-be-named " href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named">She-who-must-not-be-named </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=all-time-favourite">all-time-favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3333914848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5958551066202337156"><b> <i> Like life, what gives a story its meaning is the fact that it ends. Our stories have lives of their own—and it’s up to us to make them mean something. </i></b><br/><br/> I am reeling with a tempest of emotions of what transpired in this book. This story was everything I wanted it to be and I couldn't wish for more. It took me longer than usual to finish this book because I held onto every page, every paragraph, every word and every syllable refusing to let go. My love for this book hit a crescendo, and there is</span>
  <span id="freeText5958551066202337156" style="display:none"><b> <i> Like life, what gives a story its meaning is the fact that it ends. Our stories have lives of their own—and it’s up to us to make them mean something. </i></b><br /><br /> I am reeling with a tempest of emotions of what transpired in this book. This story was everything I wanted it to be and I couldn't wish for more. It took me longer than usual to finish this book because I held onto every page, every paragraph, every word and every syllable refusing to let go. My love for this book hit a crescendo, and there is not one thing I want to change about this book. <br /><br />Eliza Mirk is a teenager with anxiety issues, a loner who thinks she is barely a footnote in anyone's life. But online she's Lady Constellation, creator of a famous webcomic called <i> Monstrous Sea </i> and a god who creates currents in her own world. No one knows that Lady Constellation is Eliza.<br /><br /><b> <i> LadyConstellation is the hero who defeats Eliza Mirk once a week and celebrates with her many admiring fans. She is beloved by all, even the villain, because without her the villain wouldn’t exist.<br />I am LadyConstellation.<br />I am also Eliza Mirk.<br />This is the paradox that can never be solved. </i></b> <br /><br />In high school, she meets Wallace who also has a knack for her webcomic, only he doesn't know her identity too. He is the only person who understands her and a bond develops between them. But when her identity is revealed, she finds her resolve weakening and everything she built for herself starts slipping away. <br /><br />I loved the book (I probably already mentioned it, and I will continue doing so), not because I relate to Eliza or anything. I don't. If anything, we're totally different. But that didn't stop me from rooting for her. <br />I loved the book because it was magically realistic. The depiction of Eliza's hatred for school, problems with her family, social anxiety, Wallace's ability to empathise with comic characters more than real people felt completely raw and real.<br /><br />I like that Eliza and Wallace complement each other really well. They are aware of each others' flaws and accept them wholeheartedly as they open up and let each other in. They see eye-to-eye on a lot of things and are fluent in the language of  Monstrous Sea . Thanks to Wallace, Eliza gradually comes out of her shell and makes new friends and meets new people. <br /><br />I also love how her online friends stick out for her which make them more real than any real person she's ever known. Whatever I write about this book will only seem less to me and unworthy of even half of what this book has to offer. <br /><br />The blurb was so vague, I thought the story would be confined to cute romance with a lot of awkward moments and misunderstandings, but it extends much more beyond all that, signifying a lot about frienship and love and also shedding light on social issues like anxiety, depression and suicide. <br />All in all, this book is mired with wonderful yet heart rending moments intricately orchestrated into a tale that will forever be embedded into the deepest recesses of my heart. <br />Thank you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7009633.Francesca_Zappia" title="Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Francesca Zappia</a><br /><br /> <b> <i> "I am Eliza Mirk, daughter and sister and friend.<br />I am Eliza Mirk, mother of a fandom.<br />I am Eliza Mirk" </i></b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="5958551066202337156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2111423350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2111423350" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2111423350?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=contemporary-read">contemporary-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2111423350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8993937336724727673"><i>
  <b>"Like life, what gives a story its meaning is the fact that it ends. Our stories have lives of their own—and it’s up to us to make them mean something."</b>
</i><br/><br/>I think a part of me just died because this book is over. I don’t think I can process what is happening right now. I love this book so much I don’t think my heart is beating anymore. I’m still screaming my head off internally.<br/><br/>This book dealt with so many social and emotional issues with such clarity and depth I don’t think it gets better than</span>
  <span id="freeText8993937336724727673" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>"Like life, what gives a story its meaning is the fact that it ends. Our stories have lives of their own—and it’s up to us to make them mean something."</b>
</i><br /><br />I think a part of me just died because this book is over. I don’t think I can process what is happening right now. I love this book so much I don’t think my heart is beating anymore. I’m still screaming my head off internally.<br /><br />This book dealt with so many social and emotional issues with such clarity and depth I don’t think it gets better than this. The author put every word so perfectly and expressed every nook and corner of this masterpiece so eloquently it shouldn’t be possible. The story is a work of art I am enamored with and I vow to never forget it. <br /><br />Eliza Mirk is the girl who is always invisible, the person who never talks to anyone else and lives in her own world, her life is a mess.But online she is LadyConstellation the creator of a web series that went viral. She created a comic called Monstrous Sea and at this point draws like a professional. Now, there’s a new boy at her high school, Wallace, who also happens to be her most famous fanfiction writer and the only person in this school who understands her. She doesn’t tell him she’s LadyConstellation she tells him that she draws fanart and chooses to hide her true identity.<br /><br />Eliza battles with herself on issues of self worth and hides herself behind LadyConstellation. She has never tried to express herself as Eliza Mirk, she has only been LadyConstellation, the mastermind that created the most famous webcomic in existence and has never tries to be or understand herself as just Eliza.She is an introvert to the point where she can barely talk to another person. She hardly views herself as another human being amd chooses to lose herself in her work. And when I say lose herself I’m not exaggerating it takes physically pushing her off a chair to bring her feet back to the ground. She thinks that happens merely because she is dedicated to her work but she doesn't realise that she is subconsciously doing it to extract herself from the world into the world she created but to an extent in which she forgets to pay any attention to herself. I think she chose to express herself in the only method she found agreeable, through her art. Her emotions drive her to create something which reflects her feelings at the time. Eliza created her ideal world to escape into and drew it out.<br /><br />Her parents also don’t know the extent of her online life. She actually makes enough money to make a living out of her online comic. Her parents think its just a hobby and have never paid it much attention to it. I was infuriated with her parents in many parts of the story for not trusting and believing in their own daughter. They undermine her work so much and they just write her work off as a silly hobby that will get her nowhere they don't respect the fact that she is so dedicated to her work. They just <i>assume</i> that her art is nothing, just writing this makes me angry so I shall say no more.<br /><br />She has two friends online who help her manage her website and these people know her not as LadyConstellation but as Eliza Mirk and they are really close even if they do talk only online. Their conversations itself show us how clearly they could all be best friends with perfect compatibility even though they have physically never met each other. <br /><br />I <b>love</b> her brothers. Throughout the book, if you observe carefully both her brothers are so mature and have the most amazing personalities two people can have. To understand the weight that lies behind each of the words they speak we must stop looking at the situation through Eliza’s eyes and start looking at it like a bystander and then the reality of how marvelous these kids are hits you in the gut. They are not at all like Eliza, personality wise, but still found ways to understand her and accept their older sister for who she was in ways even her parents were negligent about.<br /><br />This book was not quite what I expected. I think the blurb set this theme of a cute contemporary with socially awkward people and a cute romance but there is so much going on in each of their lives, it’s a lot to process. The romance itself is a minor part of the book taken back by how much emotional and mental growth and destruction happens in this story. Each facet of this book has so much to learn from and holds quite a lot of wisdom.<br /><br />I hope I did this book justice in this review, it was a mind blowing experience and I couldn’t love it any more than I do right now. If you enjoy contemporary I definitely recommend this book to you. I give this book 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8993937336724727673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2084775756" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084775756" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2084775756?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2084775756" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4762375536578421330">[4.5 ⭐️] My heart has been wrung out. I woke up with my heart feeling so full and being in pain. I need to drown my sorrows in ice cream. Haagen Dazs Strawberry Cheesecake, preferably.<br/>Gosh, this was so relatable!<br/><br/>Pretty sure you all know what this is about, but just in case you don't, it's about Eliza and her world. The Sea Monsters. The fandom she's created and chose to write anonymously about. Her art. Which in turn becomes her life. She's more active online than she is in the real world. She's</span>
  <span id="freeText4762375536578421330" style="display:none">[4.5 ⭐️] My heart has been wrung out. I woke up with my heart feeling so full and being in pain. I need to drown my sorrows in ice cream. Haagen Dazs Strawberry Cheesecake, preferably.<br />Gosh, this was so relatable!<br /><br />Pretty sure you all know what this is about, but just in case you don't, it's about Eliza and her world. The Sea Monsters. The fandom she's created and chose to write anonymously about. Her art. Which in turn becomes her life. She's more active online than she is in the real world. She's more herself online, more at ease and anything outside of that bubble makes her uncomfortable, agitated and feel slightly overwhelmed. <br /><br />I mean, I related to this on a spiritual level. <br /><br />It did take me almost half-way to fully connect with it, but from then on, I was falling in love with it deeper and deeper. Page by page. Eliza is such a wonderful character. Her journey throughout all of this - which I'll leave out since <b>YOU SHOULD GO AND DISCOVER IT AND READ IT</b> - was intense, and agonising and healing to follow. I adored it! I understood her and I felt like I was uncovering parts of myself to myself. <br /><br />Whilst reading, there were moments of just intense connection. <i>‘Yes, I understand your anxiety. I know why you want to hide. I empathise with how you want to escape reality all the time and crawl into your safe space, because happiness resides there.’</i> It just felt all so enlightening. <br /><br />I smiled, laughed, teared up and felt the hurt through Zappia's words. The ending did feel slightly rushed. Or maybe I didn't want it to end and was craving for more, but I can absolutely see myself reading this again. When this pain heals that it.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[We have got to discuss Wallace. First of all, his email b r o k e me! So much about him made sense and I love how they both connected through Eliza's story. What has me annoyed though is how he reacted when he found out she was the creator, subsequently leading to him getting a book deal, which would only happen once Eliza completed it.<br /><br />I hated how he guilt-tripped her into trying to finish it, because it would sort out his life. I hate it! I'm still bitter about it. His apology was weak and lacked any sort of empathy. Towards the end, I was't even rooting for them anymore. I would've been happier if she actually acknowledged how he mistreated her whilst she was experiencing her anxiety and depression and dumped him.<br /><br />Her reaching out to the author was such a poignant moment and it was so admirable to see how she fought through it all. Adore this book! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4762375536578421330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2531667987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6707067014840904107"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537764600i/26344521._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You found me in a constellation.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, I loved this story. And if the ending was a little different, this would have been such an easy five star read. I love books centered on creators on the internet. While reading this, I was constantly reminded of one my favorite books of all time, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2381957292' rel='nofollow noopener'>Radio Silence</a> by Alice Oseman. Which, I’m not really sure if here is any higher praise than to be compared to that book.<br/><br/>But basically, this book is all about putting yourself out there, carving your</span>
  <span id="freeText6707067014840904107" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1537764600i/26344521._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You found me in a constellation.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, I loved this story. And if the ending was a little different, this would have been such an easy five star read. I love books centered on creators on the internet. While reading this, I was constantly reminded of one my favorite books of all time, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2381957292" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a> by Alice Oseman. Which, I’m not really sure if here is any higher praise than to be compared to that book.<br><br>But basically, this book is all about putting yourself out there, carving yourself a little home on the internet, and feeling like you belong, even if your life offline isn’t the easiest to understand. And this book follows two characters very invested with the same fandom<br><br>➽ <b>Eliza Mirk</b> - AKA: LadyConstellation, creator of one of the biggest webcomics online, <i>Monstrous Sea</i>.<br><br>➽ <b>Wallace Warland</b> - The new boy that just joined Eliza’s school halfway through senior year. Oh, and <i>Monstrous Sea</i>’s biggest fanfiction writer. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You wrote back…”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Eliza and Wallace’s paths inevitably cross, and he begins to share with her the fanfiction transcribes of the webcomic she has secretly created. And these two meeting offline was one of the most heartwarming things I’ve read all year, even though Wallace has no idea just how much Eliza is invested in this fandom. I think there is just something so beautiful about how accepting and understanding they were of the times that it’s hard to talk, or that it’s almost too much to talk. Honestly, seeing them write back and forth together, side by side, gives me more feelings than I have words for. But I loved it and thought it was so very beautiful. <br><br>This book is a love letter to the power of healing that friendships can truly have. Yet, also the healing power of fandoms and celebrating your love for something with others. The magic of finding a person you can be yourself, your true self, no masks, no fakeness, no lies, it’s something that I can’t put into words. But seeing Eliza and Wallace experience that was perfection. <br><br>But this is a story about art and how sharing your art is truly like sharing a piece of your heart. And this book really talks about how scary that can be! Yet, also how your art can inspire so many others’ art and it really can create such a beautiful cycle. <br><br>And not to bring up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2381957292" rel="nofollow noopener">Radio Silence</a> constantly, but this book also touches upon how school isn’t for everyone, no matter what people try to make you think. That there isn’t some magical step program of getting good grades in school that will lead you to an amazing university on a full-paid scholarship, which will obviously lead you to the perfect job where you will become filthy rich and experience nonstop happiness! People have so many paths they can choose from, and so many paths that are right and wrong for them. And that’s beautiful and that’s okay. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She drew so many monsters that she became a monster herself.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, I loved this book. Fandoms and having an online presence are things that I think I’ll always enjoy reading about, because it’s something very close to my heart. I will say that Wallace’s behavior at the end of this book, and the reason why he wanted Eliza to overcome it all, was just off-putting. But besides that, I loved this book. It made me soft, and warm, and ever so thankful to every single person who reads my reviews and interacts with me. Seriously, you all make me feel so blessed every single day and bring me more happiness than I can measure. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a><br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for suicidal thoughts, talk of past suicide, panic attacks, abandonment, minor bullying, talk of past loss of loved ones, grief depictions, and depression depictions. <br><br>❤ I read this for <a href="https://twitter.com/hashtag/ContemporaryAThon?src=hash" rel="nofollow noopener">Contemporary-a-thon</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6707067014840904107" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText3134476360112546517" style="display:none">UPDATE 7/10/17: I've had a lot of people ask what they can do to support and show demand for full, published versions of <i>Monstrous Sea</i> and <i>The Children of Hypnos</i>. The first Children of Hypnos book is currently available to read on Wattpad, and can be found here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/story/95478833-the-children-of-hypnos">https://www.wattpad.com/story/9547883...</a><br /><br /><i>Monstrous Sea</i> now has a short teaser also available on my Wattpad. Here's the link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/story/115593723-monstrous-sea-teaser">https://www.wattpad.com/story/1155937...</a><br /><br />Thank you all so much!<br /><br />————————————————————————<br /><br />UPDATE: If you preorder <i>Eliza and Her Monsters</i> before 5/30/17, send proof of purchase &amp; mailing address to elizapreorders@gmail.com and get a bookplate, bookmark, exclusive art, and more!
