I wrote it in the hopes that it could help other very introverted and anxious creative types and those who feel the keen double edge of fandom and life online.<br /><br />There are two other stories inside this one. The first is <i>Monstrous Sea</i>. That one's obvious. <i>Monstrous Sea</i> is my oldest story and, full disclosure, my favorite; I gave it to Eliza because it made her feelings about it real. Unfortunately, only the very tip of the <i>Monstrous Sea</i> iceberg is visible in this book, and it's not available to read anywhere. (Yet.)<br /><br />The second is Eliza's favorite book series, The Children of Hypnos, which is a real thing I wrote and am currently putting up on Tumblr and Wattpad (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.wattpad.com/story/95478833-the-children-of-hypnos">https://www.wattpad.com/story/9547883...</a>).     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2281916828" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2281916828" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2281916828?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=disability-and-mi">disability-and-mi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2281916828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7640913470634471130">I went into this book expecting greatness, honestly. A book about fandoms, anxiety, and being a child of the internet? You already know I can get behind all of that. Plus, a romance that forms through written correspondence? MY LITERAL FAVORITE TROPE? Sign me up! … Unfortunately, though, <i>Eliza</i> wasn’t <i>quite</i> everything I hoped it would be.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“I made Monstrous Sea because it's the story I wanted. I wanted a story like it, and I couldn't find one, so I created it myself.”</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>→ Eliza Mirk ←</b><br/>Eliza herself</span>
  <span id="freeText7640913470634471130" style="display:none">I went into this book expecting greatness, honestly. A book about fandoms, anxiety, and being a child of the internet? You already know I can get behind all of that. Plus, a romance that forms through written correspondence? MY LITERAL FAVORITE TROPE? Sign me up! … Unfortunately, though, <i>Eliza</i> wasn’t <i>quite</i> everything I hoped it would be.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I made Monstrous Sea because it's the story I wanted. I wanted a story like it, and I couldn't find one, so I created it myself.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Eliza Mirk ←</b><br />Eliza herself was the reason this was a 3-star read for me instead of a 5-star one. Literally, every single problem I had with this book? Eliza. Don’t get me wrong, she’s not unredeemable – she portrays fantastic anxiety rep that I related really well to, and her affinity for the webcomic she has created and its subsequent fandom reaches levels of love that I think a lot of us can understand. She’s immensely talented and a perfectionist to the point that she feels like she needs to work on her creations constantly, which is also a feeling I can get behind (hello, type A personalities!).<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Broken people don't hide from their monsters. Broken people let themselves be eaten.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ miscommunications &amp; angst ←</b><br />I don’t want anyone thinking I’m over here holding teen characters to unfair standards. I genuinely don’t mind when YA protagonists get irrationally angry at their families, or don’t want to spend time with their siblings, or lash out at friends and love interests… <i>usually.</i> Eliza, unfortunately, takes it to a new level. <br /><br />Her parents are a little bit inept and don’t have great communication, but it felt like the portrayal of their relationship was, in a sense, saying, “It’s okay to treat your parents like trash no matter how hard they try, because even if they try to understand you, they’re never going to!” We’ve all seen bad parents in YA, but the Mirks aren’t. They mess up, and they’re human, but they’re trying, and the biggest issue is, hands down, a lack of communication. While Eliza’s behavior is perfectly common for teens – especially those struggling with mental health issues – it doesn’t feel like it’s addressed or correctly quickly or well enough to justify its intensity.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You found me in a constellation.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Wallace Warland ←</b><br />The brightest spot in this book? Wallace, hands down. He’s the sort of character that you peg as the love interest from the moment he walks on to the page, but it’s hard to guess that he could be so adorable and wounded. He struggles from tremendous amounts of grief, as well as PTSD, and it manifests through his inability to speak out loud around most people (which is where the “written correspondence” trope gets its chance to shine). He is caring, kind, and so lovable, and honestly deserved better than some of the mess that Eliza put him through.<br /><br />There is a scene towards the end of the book – I won’t spoil it, but if you’ve read it, you know the one – where Eliza gives Wallace a terrible scare, and his reaction had me unexpectedly <i>sobbing</i> because he is so desperately afraid of his past repeating itself before his eyes. He was easily the character that I connected the most to, emotionally, and by the time I turned the final page, I just wanted so much more time with him.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Maybe that’s normal. The things you care most about are the ones that leave the biggest holes.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Monstrous Sea ←</b><br />One of the things I found most interesting about the book, I have to mention here: the art and snippets from Eliza’s webcomic, <i>Monstrous Sea,</i> that we get to see here and there throughout the story. The art was so fun, and it was a really nice touch that made the webcomic feel like a real-life thing – I half-expected that I would be able to go to the URLs listed and find a full, thriving forum there for a fandom I’d never known existed. The storyline snippets, on the other hand, I thought were a little dull, and didn’t form a cohesive enough mini-story to bother with trying to follow closely, but I’m happy I got the physical formatting for the illustrations alone.<br /><br /><b>→ final thoughts ←</b><br />All in all, if you enjoy books that reference internet fandoms and online friends, as well as some really solid anxiety rep, I highly recommend this book, <i>unless</i> you have a problem with angsty, self-absorbed main characters. If you think that’s a feature that you’d find yourself unable to get past, as I know is the case for many people, I’d pass on this one.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/02/21/eliza-and-her-monsters/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7640913470634471130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2117966795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2117966795" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2117966795?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117966795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8222688043011369271">i havent read a book with so much extra content since <i>‘illuminae.’</i> this totally makes me want to get into webcomics. like, how cool do they sound?! and then i need to find me a wallace so we can fangirl together. serious couple goals, right there. <br/><br/>i really liked the main story of this book, but my attention was completely drawn into the webcomic eliza created. there was so much beauty in the storyline and illustrations - i was so enthralled by it all. even though i would have loved more than the</span>
  <span id="freeText8222688043011369271" style="display:none">i havent read a book with so much extra content since <i>‘illuminae.’</i> this totally makes me want to get into webcomics. like, how cool do they sound?! and then i need to find me a wallace so we can fangirl together. serious couple goals, right there. <br /><br />i really liked the main story of this book, but my attention was completely drawn into the webcomic eliza created. there was so much beauty in the storyline and illustrations - i was so enthralled by it all. even though i would have loved more than the little glimpses given, i thought it was pretty well balanced. the comics offered great support, but didnt eclipse the main story. <br /><br />i could relate to eliza on so many levels - this book is definitely one for the introverts out there. its a really cool thing when a book is about something youve never experienced, but you relate to the character, so you feel really connected in something you know nothing about.<br /><br />i really wish this wasnt a standalone because i would read the crap out of this series. this was such a fun and sweet and interesting story! <br /><br />ps. if anyone know any good webcomics, send recommendations my way!! <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8222688043011369271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2021078887" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2021078887" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2021078887?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2021078887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2431173742929588719"><b>Unpopular opinion this way comes...</b><br/><br/>2.5 stars. I don’t think it’s normal for a book to take one hundred read pages to finally enjoy it. I wasn’t interested in reading about the online community of <i>Monstrous Sea</i> lovers, because I’m not new to fandom and most of it was repetition of what we all already know. <br/><br/>I want to be moved by the emotional experiences. Unfortunately, this takes time with this book, because Eliza keeps everything in. She suffers from anxiety. She’s also very shy and isolates her</span>
  <span id="freeText2431173742929588719" style="display:none"><b>Unpopular opinion this way comes...</b><br /><br />2.5 stars. I don’t think it’s normal for a book to take one hundred read pages to finally enjoy it. I wasn’t interested in reading about the online community of <i>Monstrous Sea</i> lovers, because I’m not new to fandom and most of it was repetition of what we all already know. <br /><br />I want to be moved by the emotional experiences. Unfortunately, this takes time with this book, because Eliza keeps everything in. She suffers from anxiety. She’s also very shy and isolates herself from her classmates. Honestly, I thought she was a boring character for at least half of the novel. <br /><br />Surely, some people will connect to her – hell, part of me did. We all have a quieter, more shy and private side. But Eliza’s ‘‘real’’ life is so monotonous. Even SHE dislikes it. Her ‘‘online’’ life is more exciting, but I personally prefer reality over what the internet brings. It’s fine to have online friends, but I disbelieve that they should be your only friends. Eliza doesn’t even want to make real life friends.<br /><br />Then she meets Wallace and it’s quite awkward between them and feels very online-ish too, what with him being unable to speak out loud and solely sharing his thoughts through writing. I’m a reader, so I love writing, but I prefer verbal communication anytime.<br /><br />It got a lot better when Eliza started discussing her problems, or at least hinting at them, when more psychological themes surfaced. Don’t read this book if what to want is to admire the webcomic pictures, because there aren’t that many of them. The <i>Monstrous Sea</i> story is definitely incomplete – it’s more of a teaser than anything else. <br /><br />All in all, it’s just too darn bad it took me so long to start enjoying it a little. I considered putting it aside a couple of times. The characters are great when they start opening up about themselves, but they never reach that point where they become extraordinary. The story is extremely underwhelming. I won’t ever reread <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31931941.Eliza_and_Her_Monsters" title="Eliza and Her Monsters by Francesca Zappia" rel="nofollow noopener">Eliza and Her Monsters</a>. I’m not that patient. It should have been condensed. No idea what the editor was thinking. Dull. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2431173742929588719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2396520178" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2396520178" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2396520178?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2396520178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7300099926625116875"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Broken people don't hide from their monsters. Broken people let themselves be eaten.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>I read this in one sitting and if that doesn't say something then I don't know what does.</b> This really was one of the most relatable and entertaining books I've ever read. There was not one moment I was bored through reading it and as it was ending, I was hoping there was more but all I got was a final art piece in the end. I was completely hooked since the beginning.<br/><br/>Eliza Mirk is the creator of the mo</span>
  <span id="freeText7300099926625116875" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Broken people don't hide from their monsters. Broken people let themselves be eaten.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>I read this in one sitting and if that doesn't say something then I don't know what does.</b> This really was one of the most relatable and entertaining books I've ever read. There was not one moment I was bored through reading it and as it was ending, I was hoping there was more but all I got was a final art piece in the end. I was completely hooked since the beginning.<br /><br />Eliza Mirk is the creator of the most famous webcomic in her time, <i>Monstrous Sea</i>, but nobody knows that. Eliza is seen and known as an introvert who scares students in her own class, the student who teachers don't call on, and the student who has no friends because no one wants to talk to her. Eliza doesn't mind that though, for she would rather spend her time looking at her computer and drawings until a full day has passed when she hasn't realized it. She then meets Wallace, who is known as <i>Rainmaker</i> online, the most famous and well-known fanfiction writer of Monstrous Sea. Wallace doesn't know Eliza is <i>LadyConstellation,</i> the creator of Monstrous Sea, and he thinks she's just another fan who has a passion for drawing fanart. As the two then begin sharing each other's love for Monstrous Sea and become closer with each other, Eliza begins to wonder if it won't hurt much to try the word offline and see what it offers. That is when her secret, her world, her creation, is shared with the whole world, and Eliza breaks the trust Wallace had in her, but she also breaks on her own, and doesn't know what to do after her secret is out.<br /><br /><b>Eliza and Her Monsters lets us know what its like to be someone who is unable to break from their shell, the life of someone who afraid of exploring the world. It lets us know what its like to face reality vs virtuality, real life vs the internet, real friends vs online friends, and the struggles of being a teenager who wants to do something she loves doing but is afraid of letting everyone know.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Maybe that’s normal. The things you care most about are the ones that leave the biggest holes.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The whole concept of this book was beautiful to me when I first read it. I had heard about Francesca Zappia's <i>Made You Up</i> back in 2015 when my friend from school told me she was reading it. She mostly reads contemporary and I always see her carrying a contemporary book that catches my eye, so when I saw Made You Up, I got interested in it. The cover for me was beautiful and the synopsis was intriguing, but I never got around to reading it. <i>Eliza and Her Monsters</i> had me wanting more Zappia and more Eliza. With that being said, <b>I know one thing for sure: This is my new favorite book out in this world.</b> Besides the creative art Eliza can do, her talent, the idea of Monstrous Sea, and meeting a cute guy who writes fanfiction who looks like a football player, <b>everything was relatable.</b> When Eliza would describe her life and situations, it felt like I was reading about myself. I didn't have to understand it to know, because I'm living it. The way Eliza developed as a character was inspiring, truly. It felt like I could do something like that—break from my shell and become a person who interacts with the world that is not online. <br /><br /><b>Social anxiety was the most relatable thing I encountered in this book.</b> Zappia could not have handled it more perfectly. The way Eliza described her social anxiety (although not really mentioned as "social anxiety") was like reading about my life. She's an introvert that would prefer staying in her room, locked, petting her 140-pound dog, watching a hilarious tv show called Dog Days or writing/drawing her creation, <i>Monstrous Sea.</i> If that doesn't explain me, I don't know what does. The difference is I don't have a talent for drawing or writing a story or coming up with creative, cool and beautiful ideas that blow up on the internet, but I would rather much stay in my room, locked, petting my 2 dogs, watching kdramas or reading. The whole concept of talking to friends but <i>online friends</i> was something anyone could relate to. Online friends are sometimes better than real life friends, and that's that. Sometimes, your real life friends don't understand you or what you're going through that you give up on asking them for advice or anything, really, that you got for your friends on a screen. It sucks that they're everywhere on the globe, which is why sometimes I wish Goodreads was at least a virtual place or a place we could go to and meet up with our friends here and talk good or shit about books. It would be pure heaven. <br /><br />One of the other things I found completely relatable was the whole anxiety and panic disorder issue. Although Eliza was not fully diagnosed with panic disorder, she showed symptoms at least once, and she started seeing a therapist that, was, actually a very good and understanding therapist. She started doing yoga with her mother because it was recommended and although it took her a while, she did it. Her character developed through the last pages, but it would really make much sense. She was a character struggling to break from her inner self and explore what is around her and the people. She didn't talk much and didn't have any friends. She wasn't shy, she just didn't care. Back to the panic disorder, I thought it was nice for Eliza to realize what it was that she was missing out on. <b>I have panic disorder and reading about how she could cope with her anxiety was something I needed to read to help myself.</b> <br /><br />This book is a 5 star read for even though there was one problem: Eliza's parents. I thought her parents were frustrating, but I could see where they were coming from. Her parents were like my parents. They would try to get her to play sports, would try to get her to walk the dog and go to a park, go to her brother's soccer game, really, do anything, even get in trouble. The problem was that her parents didn't understand the reason Eliza didn't and couldn't (at times) go out. They would always assume she was just a mean child who didn't like people. Although that was not entirely through, Eliza was someone who created a world only she knew entirely and her parents didn't understand that. Not only that, they really didn't know about Monstrous Sea. To them, it was just something Eliza did for fun, not realizing it was not a hobby but more like a passion she had. I understood where both came from. Her parents are like any other parent, wishing their child would go out and do something proactive, and Eliza was like another teenager, wishing her parents just left her alone to do her "hobby". I wish the relationship between Eliza and her family was better, but it also felt like I was reading my life so I could see why changes were made towards the end.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I understand that it's a teenage thing to say parents don't get it, but they don't get it. It's not their fault they were born two and a half decades before me, but would it kill the to ask me what I'm doing on the phone before they assume it's something pointless?</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />One of the biggest reasons I love reading YA contemporary romance is not only because of how cheesy it can be but because it's something I will never be able to relate to. I mean, why can't I just meet some cute guy who looks like he's a football player and writes fanfiction about the most famous Webcomic on the internet? Or at least, something similar. <b>All in all, Wallace was really super cute and the relationship between him and Eliza was super cute to read about.</b> I felt bad for the boy at times because of how he and Eliza interacted, but after knowing more about him, you could understand his situation. He was really someone Eliza needed, in my opinion, and the help he gave Eliza was super cute as well. Overall, their relationship and chemistry were super cute. It was all just <u>cute.</u> He was similar to Eliza, in the way where his parents didn't understand and comprehend him. They didn't understand that he was someone who had a passion for something and wanted to continue doing that because it made him happy, but he didn't have the full and unconditional support from his parents. Unsupportive parents can be the worst and really tough, but they both made it through and continued with their happy lives, doing what they love doing to make themselves the happiest. The pace their relationship took was perfect, their dialogues were super cute as well, and I don't think I've ever said super cute as much as I've said super cute in this review. He also needed to break from his inner shell and Eliza managed to help him just how he managed to help her. It took time, it took more understanding, but they did it. <br /><br /><b>Friendship in this is a major key.</b> It is what makes you realize even more that online friends are real people who are miles apart from you but are a big part of your life. Eliza didn't have friends in her real life until she met Wallace, but her real friends were Emmy and Max, the people who helped her make Monstrous Sea bigger than it was. They are the ones she relies on and trusts and although none of them have met in real life, they know she is LadyConstellation. Their dialogues were hilarious to read about. Max was definitely my favorite—the way he portrayed his character of being a Monstrous Sea male fan and his defensive conversations had me wishing he was a real person.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I do have friends. Maybe they live hundreds of miles away from me, and maybe I can only talk to them through a screen, but they're still my friends. They don't just hold Monstrous Sea together. They hold me together.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><b>Eliza and Her Monsters made me learn one thing: that you should not be afraid of who you are, of what you do, and what you want to do.</b> Zappia created unforgetting and beautiful quotes that really can touch a special place in someone's heart because of how true it can be for that person. The book can help a teen realize that its hard to be a teen that is antisocial and not someone who goes out at all. Me, for example. I don't go out at all. I hardly talk to people my age. I prefer conversations with older people because they understand more, in a way, depending on what it is that we are discussing. I would rather stay home and binge read books or shows instead of going to a wack party, spending hours of my life looking at people laugh, eat, and gossip. I would rather stay home and drink 10 cups of coffee instead of going to a party and drinking cup after cup of beer or liquor or smoking. <b>I don't care what others do as long as they don't care what I do.</b> I'm still not a social person, even on the internet, but I have more online friends than real life friends, and I will never stop living that way. I would rather meet an online friend once for a couple hours than spend so much time with a real-life friend that doesn't understand my likes and interests. <br /><br /><b>Teen life can be very dramatic and problematic, but one thing Eliza and Her Monsters can teach you is that the person itself is the one who can change it, not someone else.</b> The therapist in this novel said some wise words to Eliza that my own counselor has said to me, and it was nice hearing them again. Eliza, to me, was a beautiful yet very flawed character that needed to open her life, and she did. She currently stands as my favorite YA contemporary character. She gave me a new experience and I wish she was a real person we could all hang out with.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Like life, what gives a story its meaning is the fact that it ends. Our stories have lives of their own—and it's up to us to make them mean something.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7300099926625116875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer399603020446691427"><b>......must................<br/>........reread............<br/>..........can't............<br/>............resist.........</b><br/><br/>////////////////////////////<br/><br/><i>*I used my phone to type this review so I apologize for any mistakes or if some parts don't make sense lol*</i><br/><br/>I'm not an artist but this book made me eat, sleep and live the life of two amazing characters :') <br/>The story was just absolutely <i>beautiful</i>. It dealt with a combination of issues that we face within ourselves in our daily lives but in a very delicate manner. W</span>
  <span id="freeText399603020446691427" style="display:none"><b>......must................<br />........reread............<br />..........can't............<br />............resist.........</b><br /><br />////////////////////////////<br /><br /><i>*I used my phone to type this review so I apologize for any mistakes or if some parts don't make sense lol*</i><br /><br />I'm not an artist but this book made me eat, sleep and live the life of two amazing characters :') <br />The story was just absolutely <i>beautiful</i>. It dealt with a combination of issues that we face within ourselves in our daily lives but in a very delicate manner. We also get to read about the importance of family and how they cope with the technological world. This book also heavily emphasizes friendship... in the INTERNET WORLD. I honestly believe that we can find the <i>best</i> of friends through the internet, in many stages like: <br />- accessing a webpage or any other interactive site where people can bond over similar interests <br />- finding other interesting topics to talk about<br />- finding a comfort zone overtime and not having the need to filter things out <br />- not having the need to talk to them all. the. time.<br />- we can easily catch up without any party being annoyed with the other (at least that's how I see it lol)<br /><br />And how can I forget... based on a bunch of reviews I've skimmed, I agree that this book did the FANDOM WORLD proud! I loved reading about our main characters, Eliza and Wallace. <b>I loved reading about both of their families. I loved the comics. I loved that I was able to read a story within a story. I loved the blossoming of friendships. I loved loved loved the romance, it was subtle and sweet and I need me a Wallace.</b><br /><br />I highly recommend this book to everyone! Seriously, don't hesitate to pick it up ... you won't regret it! <br /><br />---<br /><br /><s>If an anonymous webcomic artist and fan fiction writer of that comic isn't OTP goals then IDK WHAT IS!!!<br /><br />Anyways...<br /><br />😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭IT'S HERE😭<b>IT'S HERE</b>😭</s></span>

<div id="review_2144646639" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2144646639" />
    <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2144646639?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=bf">bf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=im-all-kinds-of-shook">im-all-kinds-of-shook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2144646639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9702102472101187642"><i>Eliza and Her Monsters</i> wasn't a book I was hoping to love because I really didn't like <i>Made You Up</i> and thought they would be similar. But this book was just so highly praised and loved by everyone that I had to check it out. Everyone was a sobbing mess over it. So here I am, finished with it and sobbing because @all my mates, I get you all. <br/><br/>This book is just so hopeful, relatable and heart wrenching that I'm <i>still</i> thinking about it!!!! Honestly??? I didn't know what emotions and feelings were un</span>
  <span id="freeText9702102472101187642" style="display:none"><i>Eliza and Her Monsters</i> wasn't a book I was hoping to love because I really didn't like <i>Made You Up</i> and thought they would be similar. But this book was just so highly praised and loved by everyone that I had to check it out. Everyone was a sobbing mess over it. So here I am, finished with it and sobbing because @all my mates, I get you all. <br /><br />This book is just so hopeful, relatable and heart wrenching that I'm <i>still</i> thinking about it!!!! Honestly??? I didn't know what emotions and feelings were until I read <b>this book</b> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30038855.Letters_to_the_Lost" title="Letters to the Lost by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">Letters to the Lost</a> (totally not promoting an amazingly awesome book I loved to y'all!!!) <br /><br />From the blurb, it sounds like a cute, cheesy and geeky novel (which it kind of is), but it's so much more than that. This book shines light on how <b>online friendships/sites are healthy, normal and POSITIVE FOR PEOPLE!!!!!</b> Encouragement for choosing your own careers, doing what make <i>you</i> happy even though your peers or parents say otherwise. Positive sibling relationships and anxiety. <br /><br />This book? <b>It's awesome.</b><br /><br /><u>Plot:</u><br />Eliza Mirk is a famous teenage author of a comic online called <i>Monstrous Sea.</i> Online she is super famous and known as <i>Lady Constellation</i>, but in real life???? no one really knows her. She's shy, quiet and keeps to herself and is just Eliza Mirk. no one knows she's the famous <i>Lady Constellation</i> and she wants to keep it that way. <br /><br />Then she meets, Wallace (my son!!!) who writes amazing fanfiction for <i>Monstrous Sea</i> and together they share their love for writing, art and <i>Monstrous Sea</i>. It's all great until her identity for <i>Lady Constellation</i> is revealed and she fears everything will fuck up. <br /><br /><b>SOME MILD SPOILERS AHEAD AND THEY ARE UNMARKED.</b><br /><br /><u>WHY THIS BOOK IS AWESOME:</u><br />●<b>Online friendships are amazing</b>: Eliza Mirk spends most of her time online writing and chatting with her friends <b>of different ages</b> who she has <b>met online!!</b> She talks with them, tells her what goes on in her life and is happy with them just like a person would be with a friend who they can physically meet. <b>Online friends are <i>real friends</i></b>. I also love how people of all ages are friends here. We have a fourteen year old, a twenty one year old (I think) and a seventeen year old who are <b>so close with each other.</b><br /><br />●<b>Do what makes you happy. Never be pressured to do something you don't want and fuck the haters.</b> Wallace has a dickhead step father who I would love to punch in the face. He's always telling Wallace that his writing is "just a hobby" and he should get a proper career, one that would earn him money. Honestly, I say, do not listen to people like Wallace's step father. If writing makes someone happy and that's what they want to do for their careers? They should do that. People shouldn't stop doing what they want to please others, like @all the haters, fuck off and let us our thing. <br /><br />●<b>The characters are precious human beings that deserve everything pure in the world</b>. Nerds are just as cool as anybody else, we have a people here who love writing fanfiction, we have a person here who love writing comics and drawing, annoying, but amazing younger brothers, introverts!!! and a lost, but loyal and caring family. <br /><br />I wouldn't 100% call myself an introvert, but there are times where I don't want to socialize, get shy and want to be left alone and it's portrayed 100% accurate.<br /><br />●<b>Anxiety is a thing, people.</b> I have a lot of anxiety and I start worrying and getting scared over the smallest things that get me all worked up. It's something Eliza experiences and it's fucking relatable. This portrayal of anxiety isn't the main focus of the story, but the way Zappia blends it so casually into the story is just brilliant. <br /><br />●<b>Siblings are amazing and sometimes they can be unbearable, but let's be real we can't live without our siblings.</b> Church and Sully are amazing younger brothers. They are annoying and sometimes Eliza wants to get rid of them, but they understand you when your parents can't and they help speak up for you and are <b>always there for you</b>. <br /><br />●Eliza's family??? Not the most perfect one there. They have their arguments and disagreement, but at the end of the day, they care, love and support each other and are always there for each other. They aren't the best family out there and that's okay because many families aren't perfect. <br /><br />●Andd omg guys there's really cool art in this book and little snipets of <i>Monstrous Sea</i>. It's just really amazing<br /><br />●Something else I want to talk about is my own experience online. Not everyone has had the best experiences online and reading this book really bought up my bad online experiences. I genuinely got really upset and sad while reading this because I kept on thinking about it <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and it got really bad when Eliza was angry at her parents for exposing her identity <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. But I've also had a great time online and I wouldn't stop it for anything.<br /><br />Also, somebody find me in a constellation please and thank you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9702102472101187642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1925399000" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1925399000" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1925399000?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1925399000" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16002859926351043390">Why? Why did I take so long to finally pick this up? <br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I found you in a constellation.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>Eliza is the creator of the popular webcomic <i>Monstrous Sea</i>, online she is known as LadyConstellation. Nobody knows who LadyConstellation really is and nobody knows that Eliza Mirk <i>is</i> LadyConstellation. <br/><br/>The real world isn't as interesting to Eliza as the online one is. She doesn't know how everyone else IRL makes it seem so easy. She's shy, has social anxiety, is an introvert and finds making conversation wi</span>
  <span id="freeText16002859926351043390" style="display:none">Why? Why did I take so long to finally pick this up? <br /><br /><i>
  <b>“I found you in a constellation.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Eliza is the creator of the popular webcomic <i>Monstrous Sea</i>, online she is known as LadyConstellation. Nobody knows who LadyConstellation really is and nobody knows that Eliza Mirk <i>is</i> LadyConstellation. <br /><br />The real world isn't as interesting to Eliza as the online one is. She doesn't know how everyone else IRL makes it seem so easy. She's shy, has social anxiety, is an introvert and finds making conversation with people hard. <br /><br />She finds refuge in her art and in sharing her webcomic with a community that loves and appreciates it. <br /><br />For the first time Eliza meets a real life <i>Monstrous Sea</i> fan. Wallace is the new boy who doesn't speak. A beloved trope of mine is when two outcasts become friends. But even with Wallace Eliza doesn't share all of herself, that being the fact that she created <i>Monstrous Sea</i>.<br /><br /><blockquote>But this time it’s true, and the truth has a way of holding on. Truth is the worst monster, because it never really goes away.</blockquote><br /><br /><i>Eliza and her monsters</i> started out slow but once I got into it <b>I was hooked.</b> I read Zappia's first book <i>Made You Up</i> a few years ago and it become one of my favourite books ever. I was worried I wouldn't enjoy her second book, and my friends.... I can tell you that I worried for nothing. <br /><br />Even though Eliza and I are very different, there was still so much about her I could relate to and I could see a bit of myself in Eliza. I think many people get lost in the online world. But a lot of times it is where we find people who are like minded and who understand us better than our IRL people. <br /><br />Her friendship with Wallace was just <i>so beautiful</i>. Both of them have their own problems, but they relate to each other in a way no one else has before. I was so happy when their friendship slowly morphed into a relationship. I just love them so much *sniffles*.<br /><br />Eliza's relationship with her family is strained, with bad communication. I thought this story really represented that situation well. Where the parents don't really make an effort to know what their child loves or understand their interests. <br /><br />I just thought this book was such a brilliant example of a situation that many other people find themselves in. I would definitely recommend this book to all introverts. <br /><br />This book lingered with me days after I finished it and it even made me evaluate my own life. It made me happy and it made me cry. <br /><br /><br />While I know nothing about webcomic's and have read literally only one graphic novel, the way Zappia wrote about Monstrous Sea— Eliza and all her fans love for it— made me want to check out a webcomic. <b>If you somehow managed to get to the end of this review and you have any recommendations please let me know in the comments or leave a link.</b> I'm completely clueless 😂. <br />____<br />This book has been on the tbr for way too long 📚. <br /><br />Buddy reading with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42033066-inshirah-kamal" rel="nofollow noopener">Insh</a> 🍂</span>
  <a data-text-id="16002859926351043390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1989891890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1989891890" />
    <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs"><img alt="Tweebs♥️ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600454813p2/35431290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1989891890?book_show_action=true">Jun 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tweebs♥️ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tweebs♥️ " href="/user/show/35431290-tweebs">Tweebs♥️ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/35431290-tweebs?shelf=books-that-killed-me-and-my-ghost">books-that-killed-me-and-my-ghost</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1989891890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer302387976636792565"><b>
  <i>"You found me in a constellation."</i>
</b><br/> <br/><i>*packs my stuff*</i><br/> <br/>Y’all can find me in a constellation because I'm outta here. <br/> <br/>What is Earth?? <br/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497074878ra/22983301.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Wow. </b><br/> <br/>Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me forget the answer to 1+1. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make my skin clear. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me hear colors. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me question why no one gave me a <i>"warning" </i> <br/> <br/><b>warn·ing<br/>ˈ/wôrniNG/</b><br/> <i>- a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText302387976636792565" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"You found me in a constellation."</i>
</b><br> <br><i>*packs my stuff*</i><br> <br>Y’all can find me in a constellation because I'm outta here. <br> <br>What is Earth?? <br> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497074878ra/22983301.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Wow. </b><br> <br>Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me forget the answer to 1+1. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make my skin clear. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me hear colors. Who would’ve thought that picking this book up would make me question why no one gave me a <i>"warning" </i> <br> <br><b>warn·ing<br>ˈ/wôrniNG/</b><br> <i>- a statement or event that indicates a possible or impending danger, or problem.</i><br> <br>✓Impending danger? <i>My soul being shattered </i> <br>✓Problem? <i>Someone should've told me what I was signing up for?? </i> <br> <br><u> In other words: </u><br><br><b> Never felt so unprepared in my whole life </b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497076171ra/22983348.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's what reading this book feels like. <br><br>Seriously, I never knew I lacked anything in my life until I read this. Krytonite? Yo Superman, forget that. This book is your new weakness. It was like Francesca Zappia knew <b>exactly </b> what to write in order to kill me. Well, you know what, she succeeded. <br><br><u> Reasons why you guys should read this book</u><br><br><b>1. The plot is the bomb dot com. </b> <br><br>○ It's about Eliza Mirk who is the creator of this famous web-comic called Monstrous Sea. She goes by the name: <i>Lady Constellation. </i> She has millions of fans and followers online who practically worship her. But in real life, she's the opposite. She's an introvert, friendless, and weird. She never told anyone in her life about the fact she's the mastermind behind the web-comic. <br><br>○ Oh, the cool thing is, the author included art of the comic inside the book. Can we have a moment of silence? because yes. I love this. I love the art. Thanks for blessing our eyes. <br><br><b> 2. The characters </b> <br><br>○ I loved every single person in this book but let's be real. My two favorites are Eliza's younger brothers: <i> Sully and Church.</i> They are so precious and I want to adopt them. <br><br>○ Eliza mirk is my spirit animal. She prefers the presence of online friends rather than actual real people. I related to her so much to the point where I started to think that Francesca Zappia was writing my biography. I just loved how <b>real</b> she was. 10/10 for best character development. <br><br>○ Wallace, who is the love interest, is meh.It's not because of his name....<i>okay it's because of his name. </i> He was a great character, yeah I loved him and the romance between them because it was so cute. But when we get to a certain part in this book, I questioned him so hard like I was left thinking to myself, <i>"what's wrong with this dude??" </i> <br><br><b>3. Portrayal of Mental health </b> <br><br>○ yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes yes<br><br>○ I appreciate the fact that the mental health was the focus but it wasn't "the focus", if you get what I mean?? The author didn't go overboard. <br><br>○ They were other issues that were tackled within this book and I just love how the author handled it perfectly. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>I have a lot of love for this book and I'm going to stop here because I'm 100% sure I could go on forever listing reasons why you should read this. I highly recommend y'all read this. </i>
  <br>
</b><br><br>Francesca Zappia, please create more lovely books like these. Thank you very much :))<br><br><b>You can find this review and my other reviews at <a href="https://booksprens.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Booksprens</a> </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="302387976636792565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1827833843" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16199602409261519482">So, what is it that makes Eliza and her Monsters such an incredible book? Besides the fact that it was written by the Queen, herself ?? there are a lot of reasons. . .<br/><br/>-	<b>#1: The Characters</b><br/>-	Not only is there lots of diversity<br/>-	BUT THE CHARACTERS ARE NERDS<br/>-	We have Eliza herself as a comic artist<br/>-	A guy who writes fanfiction<br/>-	INTERNET FRIENDS<br/>-	Annoying as hell little brothers <br/>-	The introvert life<br/>-	A reasonably dysfunctional yet caring family<br/>-	The fandom life literally consumes their regular life <br/>-</span>
  <span id="freeText16199602409261519482" style="display:none">So, what is it that makes Eliza and her Monsters such an incredible book? Besides the fact that it was written by the Queen, herself ?? there are a lot of reasons. . .<br /><br />-	<b>#1: The Characters</b><br />-	Not only is there lots of diversity<br />-	BUT THE CHARACTERS ARE NERDS<br />-	We have Eliza herself as a comic artist<br />-	A guy who writes fanfiction<br />-	INTERNET FRIENDS<br />-	Annoying as hell little brothers <br />-	The introvert life<br />-	A reasonably dysfunctional yet caring family<br />-	The fandom life literally consumes their regular life <br />-	There’s nothing more I can ask for <br />-	 <br />-	<b>#2 Accurate Mental Illness Representation</b><br />-	Its not overbearing <br />-	Its mentioned in snippets that are natural and seamless to her personality<br />-	<i>I learned years ago that it’s okay to do this. To seek out small spaces for myself, to stop and imagine myself alone. People are too much sometimes...I take a moment of silence and think: <b>I am here. I am okay.</b></i><br />-	Eliza is an introvert and faces the daily bouts of anxiety that a lot of us go through without it being exaggerated <br />-	Or overwhelming to the plot <br />-	<br />-	<b>#3: Internet Friends</b><br />-	Internet friends are HILARIOUS<br />-	Even funnier than regular friends<br />-	I would know since I have <i>sooooooo</i> many<br />-	*sigh* oh right we’re getting off track<br />-	Internet friends are perfect <br />-	And Francesca portrayed that sooooo well. . .<br />-	<i> “Monstrous Sea Private Message:”<br /><b>emmersmacks:</b> So how was the turkey??<br /><b>emmersmacks:</b> Seeing as the only turkey I got was the soupy stuff they serve in the student center<br /><b>Apocalypse_Cow:</b> you could’ve asked me this in october. you know, when we canadians celebrated our thanksgiving. it was overcooked, thank you.<br /><b>emmersmacks:</b> Okay sour goose<br /><b>emmersmacks:</b> Lets hear from the less salty side of this trio </i><br /><br />-	Im living for these moments<br />-	<i> If I have my phone out talking to my online friends, they think I’m ignoring them, or being disrespectful and it’s like, no, I’m in the middle of a conversation. If you saw two people talking to each other face-to-face, you wouldn’t interrupt them and call it disrespectful, would you?” </i><br />-	 <br />-	<b>#4: Little Brothers</b><br />-	Little brothers can be the worst thing in the world<br />-	Or the best thing<br />-	Or they can be both<br />-	At the same time<br />-	It doesn’t have to make sense, little brothers defy all logic<br />-	Sully and Church was 10/10<br />-	Annoying little brothers who ruin your life<br />-	But also precious smol humans<br />-	 <br />-	<b>#5: Art</b><br />-	THERE<br />-	IS<br />-	FEATURED<br />-	ART<br />-	!!!!<br />-	ART<br />-	MADE BY FRANCESCA ZAPPIA HERSELF<br />-	ITS SO BEAUTIFUL<br />-	<br />-	I have nothing more to say than this.<br />-	Im all out of feels<br />-	Francesca Zappia, you’ve ruined my life so many times and somehow I end up loving you more for each time you do it. <br />-	Plz keep ruining my life<br />-	Im counting on you<br />-	Sincerely <br />-	Your biggest trash fan<br /><br /><i> Broken people don’t hide from their monsters. Broken people let themselves be eaten. </i><br /><br />5 stars!!!<br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br /><b>ITS HERE ITS HERE ITS HERE</b><br /><br />THERE COMES A MOMENT IN TIME WHEN YOU'RE WILLING TO CHUCK EVERY BOOK IN THE WORLD FOR A SINGLE ONE AND THIS IS MY MOMENT.<br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/29249069-pragya" rel="nofollow noopener">#2 Chessie Trash</a>((bc i'm #1))<br /><br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br /><i> 4/30/2017 update </i><br /><br />we're down to O N E fricken month, i cant wait this long plz i need this omg someone save a soul and give this to me <br /><br />((i got rejected by edelweiss i've never felt betrayal this strong))<br /><br />~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br /><br />Oh look, the queen is publishing another booK AND LOOK AT THAT COVER. Damn, imma be sitting here anxiously till I get my hands on this BEAUTY!</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3218610653?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=books-that-made-me-lose-friends">books-that-made-me-lose-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3218610653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3613006285303976771"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I lied. I said this was a book that I was either going to love or hate, that there was no middle ground... and yet here I am, in the middle ground. A lying liar, pants on fire. You see, there were things about ELIZA AND HER MONSTERS that I loved-- and things that I despised. Things that made me literally clench my teeth in fury because I was so irritated at this book and its characters. This is a very frustrating and personal read for me</span>
  <span id="freeText3613006285303976771" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/alwaysbeebooked/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I lied. I said this was a book that I was either going to love or hate, that there was no middle ground... and yet here I am, in the middle ground. A lying liar, pants on fire. You see, there were things about ELIZA AND HER MONSTERS that I loved-- and things that I despised. Things that made me literally clench my teeth in fury because I was so irritated at this book and its characters. This is a very frustrating and personal read for me. A lot of times, when I post critical reviews of books like these, I get rude comments saying, "Well, this book wasn't <i>written </i>for you." Not that that invalidates my feelings about the book, but I get where they're coming from (rudeness aside). When you're reading about a specific group and you're not <i>part </i>of that group, you don't truly know what it means to be a part of that group.<br><br><br><br>My review for ELIZA is about as #ownvoices as it gets. I used to struggle with social phobia, and I'm a content creator with anxiety. When I was in high school and college, I used to serialize my writing online. Part of the reason I have the following I do today is because a lot of my fans doing that followed me over to Goodreads and other social media sites. Like Eliza, I wrote the stories I wanted to read about but couldn't find, and I found a community that I got really active and involved with. I wouldn't presume to say that I'm as popular as she is, but I know what it feels like to have a readership that you have obligations to, and the pressure of creating content in a semi-professional way for consumers.<br><br><br><br>Like Eliza, all I wanted to do was write. I stayed in my room a lot and just wrote, sometimes for hours. I wanted to write professionally because my self-esteem was terrible and I didn't think I would ever be able to become good at anything else. Also like Eliza, I had a well-meaning family who I treated like absolute shit and villanized because they tried to push me out of my comfort zone, which made me feel threatened and afraid. I lashed out against the people who loved me because I felt like they "just didn't understand"-- but I didn't really make an effort to help them understand. Like Eliza, I just basked in my own sense of imagined injury, and poured myself into my art.<br><br><br><br>So here's the problem I have with ELIZA, and from what I've read of the other reviews, it's a problem that many people share. The anxiety rep is on point and so is the anger and the unpleasantness. But I never really feel like Eliza is ever called on her bratty behavior and her maladaptive habits. Having a mental health problem is not a free pass from personal accountability. Eliza's parents were at fault for not reaching out to her in a way that Eliza could feel comfortable with, but a lot of that was because Eliza never let herself be approached or made any attempt to get help or healthy or self-care. She used <i>Monstrous Sea </i>like a crutch, and put all her weight on it, so when it inevitably smashed, she came tumbling down because she had no other support systems in place. I could definitely see why Eliza's parents were so frustrated: she had no interest in college, didn't want to find a job, resisted going to the doctor or getting healthy, and balked at all social interactions including her family.<br><br><br><br>That is not healthy and when a hobby gets to the point that it becomes a crutch, it's time to step back. I stopped writing for a while because I felt like I had let it become an obsession. Now I feel like I've stepped back enough where I can look at it objectively and let myself enjoy it without taking offense to criticism, or feeling like I've poured my soul into it. It's something that I do for fun and enjoy, and that others enjoy as well, but my entire sense of self doesn't hinge on my creations.<br><br><br><br>There's a line in here that people shouldn't kill themselves for their art. It's spoken by Wallace, the love interest in this book. Which is REALLY FUCKING IRONIC considering what he does to Eliza after she has a mental breakdown. When he finds out someone is willing to <i>pay </i>him for the fanfic that he has written for <i>Eliza's </i>work, he DEMANDS that she finish, even though she is clearly in no psychologically healthy place to do so. SO, okay, apparently people shouldn't "kill themselves for art-- UNLESS it's of personal benefit to fucking WALLACE." Excuse you.<br><br><br><br>It's a shame, because up until that point, I really liked Wallace... but after that, there was no going back. SPEAKING OF GOING BACK-- what Eliza did to Wallace with that "scare" scene. Was. Fucking. Sickening. Up until that point, I was seething a little about the rep-- but mostly because it hit close to home and was making me think hard about a lot of my own behavior when I was Eliza's age. But after that scene... well, there was no going back. It felt like another scene of mental health being used as a "pass." Oh, I'm sorry I hurt you-- I'm not well. I'm okay now. Are you okay? WE'RE COOL. Like... considering what Wallace told her, that was such a breach of trust. And maybe she did it because he breached her own trust but man-- TOTALLY UNCALLED FOR. Yikes times infinity.<br><br><br><br>I liked the art scenes in the book but I thought the fantasy blurbs that came with them were wooden and lame. It reminded me of the fic scenes we got in Rainbow Rowell's FANGIRL, another anxiety/fandom rep that I took serious issue with. Eliza is slightly easier to relate to than Cath, who was just a hideous stereotype of every negative assumption people make about people with anxiety, wrapped in wish fulfillment fantasy and tied off with a big ol' bitch bow, but she is certainly no more likable. My favorite moment in this book was when she realizes what a twatwaffle she's been to her brothers after she learns that they have interests!!! and are actually people like her!!!<br><br><br><br>Jesus Christ, Eliza. How self-centered can you get.<br><br><br><br>I'm not sure if it's intentional, but I think that self-centered element is another part of anxiety and depression that isn't often talked about but it's hard to focus on others when you feel bad inside. Eliza feels crappy and dwells on that, so she doesn't really think about her family or her friends as having any problems, and the way she used her friends as personal therapists was kind of unhealthy, too. I felt like the book was trying to show that when she texts her friends during her breakdown and they don't write back because they're busy!! having lives!! but this also was never really addressed, and I think it is something that really is important. Healthy relationships where care is reciprocated.<br><br><br><br>I said more than I meant to say about this book but it made me feel a lot of things pretty strongly. I wouldn't read it again because I feel like the overall message in this book hurts more than it helps, and I kind of hate that Eliza was never taken to task for all the bad things she did and Wallace basically got off scot-free for being a raging shit weasel. The last 20% of the book ruined everything that was cute about their interactions in the first 80% and Eliza's treatment of her family even cast a shadow over that. So, that's my #ownvoices perspective. Not all rep is created equal, so maybe you'll see yourself in her more favorably than I did. But if you're going to tell me that I read the book wrong, or that it wasn't written for me, we can chat later via 1-800-GIRL-BYE at never o' clock.<br><br><br><br>2.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="3613006285303976771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2005761807" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2005761807" />
    <a title="emi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34410191-emi"><img alt="emi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603747413p2/34410191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2005761807?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emi" href="/user/show/34410191-emi">emi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=i-spent-my-money-on-this">i-spent-my-money-on-this</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=2017">2017</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=girl-meets-boy-contemporaries">girl-meets-boy-contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34410191-emi?shelf=please-read-this">please-read-this</a>,
